## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic corpus formulas stand where the lineage's thesis is stated in the skill's overview line, the hard part is keeping declarative UI, scene mutation, async data, and performance in the right lanes, naming the domain's core tension, React's declarative rerender model and Three.js's mutable per-frame world are opposed paradigms sharing one page, and the discipline is boundary management, not framework mastery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the tension is structural, React reconciles trees on state change while a 60fps scene mutates objects thousands of times between changes, letting either paradigm govern the other's territory produces the two canonical failures, rerender storms and stale scenes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the naive integration puts scene objects in React state, every frame becomes a state update, every update a reconciliation, the app shell rerendering at animation frequency, the failure the agent's guardrails and the anchor's section 8.2 both name

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed one generic engineer stands where the natural journey is the Parseltongue build the agent was written for, a developer receives a diff-visualization task, splits state into lanes, types the transport payloads and writes the adapter, builds the store with an actions object, mounts the force-graph canvas with color-coded change types, wires the WebSocket hook with reconnect refs, then walks the checklist, selection across refresh, camera reset, teardown, fallback, and pins the shell with Playwright specs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the journey works because each artifact isolates one lane, the adapter absorbs transport shape, the store absorbs app state, the canvas component stays a pure scene consumer, and the hooks own their lifecycles, so growth in any lane stays in its lane
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey's classic derailment is skipping the adapter under schedule pressure, raw snake_case payloads flow into mesh code, and every backend field rename becomes a scene-layer hunt, the shortcut converting one file of mapping into permanent coupling
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: journeys through this lineage's practice, corpus-process journeys stay in the seed lines
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the scenario as the diff-graph build with the lane split as its spine
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the journey's order is load-bearing, data model before visuals is the skill's step three, and the agent's file tree encodes it, types and adapters exist before components consume them, reversing the order to get pixels early is the path to the giant canvas, the lineage's journey is a dependency order wearing a narrative

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's evidence bullets stand while the lineage's own observability surface goes unnamed, connection status as a first-class UI indicator with its own component and testid, console error counts as an e2e signal, rerender inspection via devtools as the lane auditor, and the skill's degraded states doubling as observability, every abnormal condition owning a visible rendering rather than a silent log line

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's p95-and-screenshots packet stands while the lineage's performance doctrine goes unstated, the agent's five tips, memoized callbacks, store selectors, debounced socket events, list virtualization, and lazy-loading the 3D bundle, the checklist's volume questions, cached derived metrics, culled labels, degrading geometry, reused materials, and the anchor's whole sections on instancing, pooling, and delta-clamped render loops
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because performance work here splits by lane, React-side costs answer to memoization and selectors, scene-side costs answer to instancing and culling, and the socket layer answers to debouncing, one budget spent in three currencies
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: optimizing the wrong lane wastes the effort, memoizing callbacks cannot save a scene drowning in per-frame allocations, and instancing cannot save a shell rerendering on every hover, diagnosis before optimization is the method
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: performance doctrine from the sources, the seed's measurement packet remains the reporting format
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to organize the method by lane, attribute the cost first, then apply the lane's own toolkit
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the lineage's performance advice is scale-conditional throughout, the checklist asks whether geometry can degrade and labels cull at high counts rather than prescribing them, encoding that premature scene optimization is real, the toolkit activates at measured thresholds, not at design time, measurement as the trigger rather than the afterthought

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's distributed-execution paragraphs stand while the lineage's own scale limits go unnamed, the lane model governs one React app with one canvas boundary, multi-canvas dashboards multiply scene lanes without new doctrine, the checklist's volume questions bound the force-graph approach itself, beyond some node count no culling saves a naive force layout, and the doctrine says nothing about server-side rendering, native targets, or worker-offloaded physics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the sources were written for one product's single-canvas graph explorer, their boundaries are the product's, and the doctrine generalizes exactly as far as the lane structure holds, one declarative shell around one imperative scene
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the characteristic overreach is treating the force graph as infinitely scalable because the checklist mentions degradation, degradation strategies extend the ceiling, they do not remove it, past the ceiling the answer is aggregation or a different visualization, not more culling
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the lineage's doctrine, corpus-execution splitting stays in the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three boundaries, single-canvas doctrine, force-graph ceilings, and the unaddressed rendering targets
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the lane model scales by replication rather than extension, each additional canvas gets its own scene lane with the same rules, so dashboards need lane instances, not new doctrine, the model's real boundary is not canvas count but the assumption that React owns the shell, invalidated only when the host paradigm changes
